## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from exponential and logistic growth to more complex models with Allee effects, time-varying parameters, and density-dependent feedback.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerating logarithmically near capacity)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * P * (1 - c1 * P) (per-capita growth rate increasing at low density)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Time-dependent logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (carrying capacity or growth rate changing with time)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent growth with proportional removal)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth curve)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal or cyclic environmental variation)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (saturating per-capita growth rate)
- Power-law density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (nonlinear scaling of growth with population)
- Exponential decay with time modulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Rational Allee-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * P / (P + c2) (Allee effect via hyperbolic term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Quadratic dependence on P (P - PÂ²) â†’ logistic-type density-dependent regulation with a carrying capacity
- Cubic dependence on P (PÂ² - PÂ³ or PÂ² - P) â†’ Allee effect where growth is negative at very low populations
- Logarithmic coupling log(c/P) â†’ Gompertz-type growth with slower approach to saturation than logistic
- Multiplicative time-dependent factor (1 + f(t)) on growth rate â†’ environmental forcing or seasonality
- Ratio P/(P + c) â†’ type II functional response or weak Allee effect creating density-dependent per-capita rate
- Product of two linear factors in P â†’ bistability or multiple equilibria in population dynamics
- Exponential function of time multiplying P â†’ non-autonomous growth with secular trend in environment
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 â†’ sub-linear growth scaling typical of resource-limited colonial organisms
- Sinusoidal function of time â†’ periodic environmental drivers like seasons affecting birth/death rates
- Negative constant term independent of P â†’ constant-rate harvesting or immigration creating threshold dynamics
